CC   -!- FUNCTION: Beta-glycosidase that catalyzes the transfer of glucose
CC       moiety to anthocyanidin 3-glucoside at the 5 position.
CC       Anthocyanins are ubiquitous colored pigments that are responsible
CC       for variations in petal color. Uses acyl-glucoses, but not UDP-
CC       glucose, as the glucose donor.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: 1-O-sinapoyl-beta-D-glucose + cyanidin 3-O-
CC       beta-D-glucoside = sinapate + cyanidin 3,5-di-O-beta-D-glucoside.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=13 mM for cyanidin 3-glucopyranoside (with native enzyme at
CC         pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius);
CC         KM=46.5 mM for 1-O-beta-D-vanillyl-glucose (with native enzyme
CC         at pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius);
CC         KM=6.5 mM for cyanidin 3-glucopyranoside (with recombinant
CC         enzyme at pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius);
CC         KM=51.9 mM for 1-O-beta-D-vanillyl-glucose (with recombinant
CC         enzyme at pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius);
CC         Note=Kcat is 0.06 sec(-1) with cyanidin 3-glucopyranoside (with
CC         native enzyme at pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius). Kcat is 0.01
CC         sec(-1) with 1-O-beta-D-vanillyl-glucose (with native enzyme at
CC         pH 5.0 and 30 degrees Celsius). Kcat is 0.07 sec(-1) with
CC         cyanidin 3-glucopyranoside (with recombinant enzyme at pH 5.0
CC         and 30 degrees Celsius). Kcat is 0.01 sec(-1) with 1-O-beta-D-
CC         vanillyl-glucose (with recombinant enzyme at pH 5.0 and 30
CC         degrees Celsius);
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 4.5-5.0;
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 48 degrees Celsius;
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Pigment biosynthesis; anthocyanin biosynthesis.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Vacuole.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in petals.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expression peaks at stage 2 of petal
CC       development.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Petal color variations. Petals accumulate
CC       anthocyanin lacking the glucosyl moiety at the 5 position.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 1 family.

CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: L-asparagine + H(2)O = L-aspartate + NH(3).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=0.27 mM for L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.27 mM for D-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.27 mM for N-acetyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.07 mM for N-carbamyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.06 mM for N-isoleucyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.06 mM for N-glycyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.06 mM for N-valyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.2 mM for N-methionyl-L-asparagine;
CC         KM=0.4 mM for N-glycyl-D-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=42 umol/min/mg enzyme for L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=60 umol/min/mg enzyme for D-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=167 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-acetyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=79 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-carbamyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=67 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-isoleucyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=135 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-glycyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=56 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-valyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=92 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-methionyl-L-asparagine;
CC         Vmax=8 umol/min/mg enzyme for N-glycyl-D-asparagine;
CC         Note=Does not act on isoasparagine, L-aspartate diamide, beta-
CC         alanine amide and L-glutamine;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 6.8. Active from pH 5.5 to pH 7.5. Stable from pH
CC         3.5 to pH 10.5;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted. Periplasm.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Subject to nitrogen catabolite repression (NCR). Not
CC       found in cells grown on rich nitrogen sources like ammonia,
CC       glutamine or glutamate, but is found in cells that have been
CC       subjected to nitrogen starvation or have been grown on a poor
CC       nitrogen source such as proline.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Yeast contains 2 L-asparaginase isoenzymes:
CC       cytoplasmic L-asparaginase I, and cell wall L-asparaginase II.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: There are 4 copies for L-asparaginase 2 in yeast.
CC       The 4 identical copies ASP3-1, ASP3-2, ASP3-3 and ASP3-4 are
CC       arranged in tandem repeats located near a ribosomal DNA cluster.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the asparaginase 1 family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the stereoselective oxidative cyclization of
CC       the monoterpene moiety in cannabigerolic acid (CBGA), producing
CC       cannabidiolate (CBDA), the major cannabioid in fiber-type Cannabis
CC       plants. Can also use cannabinerolic acid as substrate, but not
CC       cannabigerol or cannabinerol.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Cannabigerolate + O(2) = cannabidiolate +
CC       H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by Hg(2+).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=0.137 mM for cannabigerolic acid;
CC         KM=0.206 mM for cannabinerolic acid;
CC         Vmax=2.57 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with cannabigerolic acid as
CC         substrate;
CC         Vmax=0.39 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with cannabinerolic acid as
CC         substrate;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 5.0;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted. Secreted, extracellular space,
CC       apoplast (By similarity). Note=Probably sorted from the secretory
CC       cells into the storage cavity of glandular trichomes.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in young leaves.
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: CBDA synthase might contribute to the self-defense
CC       of Cannabis plants by producing both CBDA and hydrogen peroxide,
CC       but since these reaction products are toxic to the plant itself,
CC       CBDA synthase is probably secreted from secretory cells into the
CC       storage cavity to avoid cellular damage (By similarity).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the oxygen-dependent FAD-linked
CC       oxidoreductase family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 FAD-binding PCMH-type domain.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Glucuronoyl esterase which may play a significant role
CC       in biomass degradation, as it is considered to disconnect
CC       hemicellulose from lignin through the hydrolysis of the ester bond
CC       between 4-O-methyl-D-glucuronic acid residues of glucuronoxylans
CC       and aromatic alcohols of lignin. Does not hydrolyze substrates of
CC       other carbohydrate esterases such as acetylxylan esterase, acetyl
CC       esterase and feruloyl esterase.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=0.5 mM for 4-nitrophenyl 2-O-(methyl-4-O-methyl-a-D-
CC         glucopyranosyluronate)-b-D-xylopyranoside;
CC         Vmax=5.5 umol/min/mg enzyme toward 4-nitrophenyl 2-O-(methyl-4-
CC         O-methyl-a-D-glucopyranosyluronate)-b-D-xylopyranoside;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 5.5;
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 40-60 degrees Celsius;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted (Probable).
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Induced in the presence of lactose or sophorose.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the carbohydrate esterase 15 family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 CBM1 (fungal-type carbohydrate-binding)

RC   STRAIN=cv. Columbia;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Dirigent proteins impart stereoselectivity on the
CC       phenoxy radical-coupling reaction, yielding optically active
CC       lignans from two molecules of coniferyl alcohol in the
CC       biosynthesis of lignans, flavonolignans, and alkaloids and thus
CC       plays a central role in plant secondary metabolism.
CC       Enantiocomplementary dirigent protein that mediates the laccase-
CC       catalyzed enantioselective oxidative phenol coupling of (E)-
CC       coniferyl alcohol to (-)-pinoresinol.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Self; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-7796038, EBI-7796038;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted, extracellular space, apoplast
CC       (Probable).
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in roots, cotyledon veins, leaf
CC       trichomes, flowers, siliques, and meristems. Present in
CC       interfascicular/vascular cambia and developing xylem.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: In flowers, expressed in the vasculature of
CC       petals, stamen filaments, anther microsporangia, and papillar
CC       cells of the stigma and style. In siliques, accumulates in the
CC       stigmatic region, replum, funiculus, and valve.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the plant dirigent protein family.

RA   Greiner-Tollersrud L., Berg T., Stensland H.M., Evjen G.,
RA   Greiner-Tollersrud O.K.;
RT   "Bovine brain myelin glycerophosphocholine choline phosphodiesterase
RT   is an alkaline lysosphingomyelinase of the eNPP-family, regulated by
RT   lysosomal sorting.";
RL   Neurochem. Res. 38:300-310(2013).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Choline-specific glycerophosphodiester
CC       phosphodiesterase. The preferred substrate may be
CC       lysosphingomyelin. Also hydrolyzes lysophosphatidylcholine (LPC)
CC       to form monoacylglycerol and phosphorylcholine but not
CC       lysophosphatidic acid, showing it has a lysophospholipase C
CC       activity. Has a preference for LPC with short (12:0 and 14:0) or
CC       polyunsaturated (18:2 and 20:4) fatty acids. Also hydrolyzes
CC       glycerophosphorylcholine and sphingosylphosphorylcholine
CC       efficiently. Hydrolyzes the classical substrate for phospholipase
CC       C, p-nitrophenyl phosphorylcholine in vitro, while it does not
CC       hydrolyze the classical nucleotide phosphodiesterase substrate, p-
CC       nitrophenyl thymidine 5'-monophosphate. Does not hydrolyze diacyl
CC       phospholipids such as phosphatidylethanolamine,
CC       phosphatidylinositol, phosphatidylserine, phosphatidylglycerol and
CC       phosphatidic acid (By similarity).
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: A lysophosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = a
CC       monoacylglycerol + phosphocholine.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: sn-glycero-3-phosphocholine + H(2)O = glycerol
CC       + phosphocholine.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Divalent cations (By similarity).
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by EDTA and EGTA in vitro (By
CC       similarity).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=2000 uM for lysophosphatidylcholine;
CC         KM=5000 uM for glycerophosphocholine;
CC         KM=35 uM for p-nitrophenylphosphocholine;
CC         KM=5 uM for lysosphingomyelin;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Lipid-anchor, GPI-anchor.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the nucleotide
CC       pyrophosphatase/phosphodiesterase family.

RP   PHARMACEUTICAL.
RX   PubMed=21184772; DOI=10.1016/j.toxicon.2010.12.010;
RA   Earl S.T., Masci P.P., de Jersey J., Lavin M.F., Dixon J.;
RT   "Drug development from Australian elapid snake venoms and the Venomics
RT   pipeline of candidates for haemostasis: Textilinin-1 (Q8008),
RT   Haempatch (Q8009) and CoVase (V0801).";
RL   Toxicon 59:456-463(2012).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake prothrombin activator that attacks the hemostatic
CC       system of prey. This non-catalytic subunit is functionally similar
CC       to blood coagulation factor V. It serves as a critical cofactor
CC       for the prothrombinase activity of the catalytic subunit, which is
CC       similar to the blood coagulation factor X.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of a light and a heavy chains; non-disulfide-
CC       linked. The interaction between the two chains is calcium-
CC       dependent (By similarity). Found in its active form associated
CC       with pseutarin-C catalytic subunit (AC Q56VR3).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: In physiological conditions, blood coagulation factor V and
CC       factor Va are inactivated by activated protein C (APC) through
CC       proteolytic degradation of the heavy chain. However, pseutarin-C
CC       non-catalytic subunit (factor V-like protein) retains its full
CC       activity even at high concentration of APC. This has two
CC       explanations: this protein has only one of the three cleavage
CC       sites present in factor V that are targeted by the APC for
CC       inactivation, and the binding with the catalytic subunit protect
CC       the cleavage site from inactivation.
CC   -!- PHARMACEUTICAL: Is under preclinical trial by the Australian
CC       biopharmaceutical company QRxPharma Ltd, its subsidiary Venomics
CC       Pty Ltd (VPL) and the University of Queensland (UQ) under the name
CC       CoVase (V0801). Tested as a procoagulant cofactor that may have
CC       application as a systemic anti-bleeding agent in the treatment of
CC       internal bleeding and non-compressible haemorrhage.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: In contrast to blood coagulation factors that
CC       circulate as inactive zymogen in plasma, venom prothrombin
CC       activators are always found in the active form in the venom.
CC       Hence, catalytic and non-catalytic subunits are found naturally in
CC       venom as stable complexes.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the multicopper oxidase family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 3 F5/8 type A domains.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 2 F5/8 type C domains.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 6 plastocyanin-like domains.

RX   PubMed=17385891; DOI=10.1021/bi062139d;
RA   Rogers M.S., Tyler E.M., Akyumani N., Kurtis C.R., Spooner R.K.,
RA   Deacon S.E., Tamber S., Firbank S.J., Mahmoud K., Knowles P.F.,
RA   Phillips S.E.V., McPherson M.J., Dooley D.M.;
RT   "The stacking tryptophan of galactose oxidase: a second-coordination
RT   sphere residue that has profound effects on tyrosyl radical behavior
RT   and enzyme catalysis.";
RL   Biochemistry 46:4606-4618(2007).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the sterospecific oxidation of primary
CC       alcohols to the corresponding aldehydes. The biologically relevant
CC       substrate of the enzyme is not known as the enzyme exhibits broad
CC       substrate specificity from small alcohols through sugars to oligo-
CC       and polysaccharides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: D-galactose + O(2) = D-galacto-hexodialdose +
CC       H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 Cu(2+) ion per subunit.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by diethyldithiocarbamate.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=56 mM for 1-methyl-alpha-D-galactopyranoside;
CC         KM=57 mM for 2-methylene-1,3-propanediol;
CC         KM=68 mM for D-galactose;
CC         KM=2.5 M for D-fructose;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 7. Active from pH 5.7 to 9.4;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- PTM: Galactose oxidase contains a protein-derived free radical
CC       cofactor. In the active state, Tyr-313, which is cross-linked to
CC       Cys-269 via a thioether bond, is oxidized to a radical and acts
CC       with Cu(2+) as a two-electron acceptor in the oxidation reaction.
CC       The cross-link is believed to modulate the redox potential of the
CC       tyrosyl radical, which is further stabilized by a stacking
CC       interaction with Trp-331 in the active site. The post-
CC       translational formation of the cross-link is closely linked to the
CC       propeptide cleavage event, and both are copper-dependent,
CC       autocatalytic processes. The propeptide may act as an
CC       intramolecular chaperone, facilitating thioester bond formation
CC       and copper binding by positioning of active-site residues,
CC       including copper ligands.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=68520; Method=Electrospray; Range=42-680;
CC       Source=PubMed:15047910;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 F5/8 type C domain.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 5 Kelch repeats.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Was originally thought to originate from Polyporus
CC       circinatus then later from Dactylium dendroides and is now known
CC       to be originating from Gibberella (Fusarium).
CC   -!- WEB RESOURCE: Name=Worthington enzyme manual;
CC       URL="http://www.worthington-biochem.com/GAO/";

CC   -!- FUNCTION: This three-finger toxin shows a potent analgesic effect
CC       against acute and inflammatory pain upon central and peripheral
CC       injection. It acts through a reversible block of the heteromeric
CC       channel ASIC1a-ASIC2a (ACCN2-ACCN1) in central neurons and of
CC       ASIC1b-containing channels in nociceptors. Acts as a gating
CC       modifier toxin by binding to the closed/inactivated channel. On
CC       channels expressed in COS-7 cells, it shows IC(50) of: 55 nM on
CC       rASIC1a, 127 nM on hASIC1a, 246 nM on rASIC1a-rASIC2a, 61 nM on
CC       rASIC1a-rASIC2b, 192 nM on ASIC1b, and 72 nM on rASIC1a-rASIC1b.

CC       Note=Average mass; Source=PubMed:23034652;
CC   -!- PHARMACEUTICAL: Promising peptide that shows a potent analgesic
CC       effect against acute and inflammatory pain that can be as strong
CC       as morphine but resistant to naloxone, with much less tolerance
CC       and no respiratory distress.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Has no effect on ASIC2a (ACCN1), ASIC3 (ACCN3),
CC       ASIC1a-ASIC3 (ACCN2-ACCN3) and ASIC1b-ASIC3 (ACCN2-ACCN3)
CC       channels, as well as on TRPV1, P2RX2 (P2X2), HTR3A (5-HT3A),
CC       Nav1.8 (SCN10A), Cav3.2 (CACNA1H) and Kv1.2 (KCNA2) channels. Does
CC       not produce motor dysfunction, apathy, flaccid paralysis,
CC       convulsions or death upon central injections (intrathecal or
CC       intracerebroventricular) in mice (PubMed:23034652).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the snake three-finger toxin family.

RP   FUNCTION, TISSUE SPECIFICITY, AND DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE.
RX   PubMed=20665709; DOI=10.1002/jez.b.21366;
RA   Bardet C., Vincent C., Lajarille M.C., Jaffredo T., Sire J.Y.;

RT   also expressed in bone cells.";

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Major component of the eggshell matrix. May play an
CC       important role in the regulation of calcite growth during eggshell
CC       calcification. May also regulate the mineralization process in
CC       developing and growing bones.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted, extracellular space, extracellular
CC       matrix. Note=Synthesized and secreted by the granular epithelial
CC       cells of the uterus and incorporated into the eggshell matrix.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: In the eggshell, expressed mainly in the
CC       palisade and mammillary layers. Expression also detected in the
CC       hypertrophic zone of the epiphyseal growth plate, and in cortical
CC       and medullary bone (at protein level). Highly expressed in uterus.
CC       Not detected in the proximal oviduct, liver, magnum, duodenum and
CC       kidney.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed at high levels at the middle of the
CC       calcification stage of shell formation. Expression levels are
CC       similar at 3-4 hours post-oviposition prior to entry of the egg
CC       into the uterus and at 16-17 hours post-oviposition during
CC       eggshell calcification. Expressed in tibia from E5 and in mandible
CC       from E7 until the end of embryonic development at E19. Expression
CC       detected first in osteoblasts, in later stages both in osteoblasts
CC       and osteocytes, and by the end of embryonic development mainly in
CC       osteocytes.
CC   -!- PTM: Asn-62 is fully glycosylated, whereas only less than 10% of
CC       Asn-293 seem to be glycosylated.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the osteoregulin family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes an oxidative deamination of predominantly
CC       hydrophobic and aromatic L-amino acids (L-Leu), thus producing
CC       hydrogen peroxide that may contribute to the diverse toxic effects
CC       of this enzyme. Exhibits diverse biological activities, such as
CC       hemolysis, edema, hemorrhage, apoptosis, antibacterial and
CC       antiparasitic activities, as well as regulation of platelet
CC       aggregation. Effects of snake L-amino oxidases on platelets are
CC       controversial, since they either induce aggregation or inhibit
CC       agonist-induced aggregation. These different effects are probably
CC       due to different experimental conditions (By similarity).
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: An L-amino acid + H(2)O + O(2) = a 2-oxo acid
CC       + NH(3) + H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: FAD (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; non-covalently linked (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated. Glycosylation is needed for activity (By
CC       similarity).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the flavin monoamine oxidase family. FIG1
CC       subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the oxidative deamination of positively
CC       charged L-amino acids L-Lys and L-Arg and, much less efficiently,
CC       of amino acids L-His and L-Tyr. Has antimicrobial activity.
CC       Inhibits growth of Gram-negative bacteria E.coli strain MC4100
CC       (MIC=0.62 ug/ml), E.coli strain C921-b2, S.typhimurium strain AA
CC       140 (MIC=0.62 ug/ml), P.aeruginosa strain PAO1 (MIC=0.31 ug/ml)
CC       and V.harveyi strain BB170 (MIC=0.25 ug/ml). Inhibits growth of
CC       Gram-positive bacteria S.aureus stain 6835 (MIC=0.31 ug/ml),
CC       S.pyogenes strain NZ131 (MIC=0.62 ug/ml), B.subtilis strain 168
CC       (MIC=2.50 ug/ml) and B.subtilis strain WB600 (MIC=2.50 ug/ml). The
CC       antibacterial effect can be bacteriostatic, mediated mostly by
CC       H(2)O(2), as well as bactericidal. The latter appears to be due to
CC       unstable intermediates generated from alpha-keto-epsilon-
CC       aminocaproic acid, an intermediate of escapin-deaminated L-Lys,
CC       and H(2)O(2). The bactericidal effect is stronger at lower pH
CC       levels. Intermediates generated from L-Arg have no bactericidal
CC       effect. Inhibits growth of yeast species S.cerevisiae strain
CC       BY4761 (MIC=5.0 ug/ml) and C.krusei (MIC=5.0 ug/ml). Inhibits
CC       growth of C.sphaerospermum in a lysine-dependent manner. As
CC       components of ink, products from escapin's enzymatic activity may
CC       play a role in deterring eukaryotic predators.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: An L-amino acid + H(2)O + O(2) = a 2-oxo acid
CC       + NH(3) + H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: FAD.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=85.5 uM for L-Lys;
CC         KM=120.5 uM for L-Arg;
CC         Vmax=4.5 umol/sec/ug enzyme with L-Lys as substrate;
CC         Vmax=5.5 umol/sec/ug enzyme with L-Arg as substrate;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed exclusively in the ink gland. Within
CC       the ink gland, it is only detected in amber vesicles (at protein
CC       level).
CC   -!- PTM: Not glycosylated.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the flavin monoamine oxidase family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes an oxidative deamination of predominantly
CC       hydrophobic and aromatic L-amino acids (highly against L-Met, L-
CC       Leu, L-Phe and L-Ile), thus producing hydrogen peroxide that may
CC       contribute to the diverse toxic effects of this enzyme. Exhibits
CC       diverse biological activities, such as antibacterial on both Gram-
CC       positive and Gram-negative bacteria and antiparasitic activities,
CC       as well as induction of platelet aggregation. Effects of snake L-
CC       amino oxidases on platelets are controversial, since they either
CC       induce aggregation or inhibit agonist-induced aggregation. These
CC       different effects are probably due to different experimental
CC       conditions. This protein may also have activities in hemorrhage,
CC       hemolysis, edema, and apoptosis.

CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated (Probable). The enzymatic activity is not
CC       affected by deglycosylation.

CC       a result of enzyme-catalyzed hydrogen peroxide production

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes an oxidative deamination of predominantly
CC       hydrophobic and aromatic L-amino acids (L-Tyr followed by L-Phe,
CC       L-Met, L-Leu, L-Trp), thus producing hydrogen peroxide that may
CC       contribute to the diverse toxic effects of this enzyme. Inhibits
CC       ADP- and collagen-induced platelet aggregation. This inhibition is
CC       inhibited by catalase, indicating the importance of generated
CC       H(2)O(2) for the inhibitory effect. This effect on platelets among
CC       snake L-amino-acid oxidases is however controversial, since some
CC       of them induce aggregation, whereas the other inhibit agonist-
CC       induced aggregation. In vivo, this enzyme induces a rapid,
CC       substantial and reversible increase in the paw volume of mice
CC       (edema). In addition, myofibrosis, and inflammatory cell
CC       infiltration on the paw tissue are also observed.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: An L-amino acid + H(2)O + O(2) = a 2-oxo acid
CC       + NH(3) + H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: FAD (By similarity).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:

CC         KM=0.142 mM for L-Phe (at pH 7.5 and 25 degrees Celsius);
CC         KM=0.373 mM for L-Met (at pH 7.5 and 25 degrees Celsius);
CC         KM=0.318 mM for L-Trp (at pH 7.5 and 25 degrees Celsius);

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes an oxidative deamination of predominantly
CC       hydrophobic and aromatic L-amino acids, thus producing hydrogen
CC       peroxide that may contribute to the diverse toxic effects of this
CC       enzyme. Exhibits diverse biological activities, such as
CC       hemorrhage, hemolysis, edema, apoptosis of vascular endothelial
CC       cells or tumor cell lines, antibacterial and antiparasitic
CC       activities (By similarity). This protein induces platelet
CC       aggregation by both hydrogen peroxide production and binding to
CC       platelet membrane proteins (that would enhance the sensitivity of
CC       platelets to hydrogen peroxide). Effects of snake L-amino oxidases
CC       on platelets are controversial, since they either induce
CC       aggregation or inhibit agonist-induced aggregation. These
CC       different effects are probably due to different experimental
CC       conditions.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: An L-amino acid + H(2)O + O(2) = a 2-oxo acid
CC       + NH(3) + H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: FAD (By similarity).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         Vmax=38.4 umol/min/mg enzyme;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; non-covalently linked (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated (By similarity).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the flavin monoamine oxidase family. FIG1
CC       subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that inhibits human
CC       platelet aggregation induced by ADP, collagen and epinephrin
CC       (possibly by binding the platelet receptor alpha-IIb/beta-III) and
CC       induces mild edema in the foot pads of mice. PLA2 catalyzes the
CC       calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=1.66 mM for phospholipids;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 7.5;
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 37 degrees Celsius;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Is non-lethal to mice and devoid of neurotoxicity,
CC       myotoxicity, hemorrhage, anticoagulant activity and cytotoxicity
CC       (PubMed:10519645).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 that causes internal
CC       bleeding, shows very strong anticoagulant activities and inhibits
CC       ADP-induced platelet aggregation. Shows very low cytotoxicity.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13547.9; Method=MALDI; Range=17-137;
CC       Source=PubMed:21185324;
CC   -!- TOXIC DOSE: LD(50) is 10.7 mg/kg by intraperitoneal injection into
CC       mice.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Two proteins (Vur-PL2A and Vur-PL2B) with different
CC       masses and detected in two different fractions have been isolated
CC       from the venom. They both seem to have the same sequence. Vur-PL2B
CC       is possibly a more stable conformer than Vur-PL2A. Since data on
CC       both proteins are very similar, information reported here only
CC       concern Vur-PL2B.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Monomer: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that shows
CC       an PLA2 activity of 578 umol/min/mg.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Heterodimer (A and B chains): snake venom phospholipase
CC       A2 that shows a PLA2 activity of 1377 umol/min/mg. Acts as a
CC       presynaptic neurotoxin. In vivo, induces edema and produces
CC       neurotoxic symptoms in mice. It exhibits indirect hemolysis and a
CC       strong myonecrotic activity and is cytotoxic. PLA2 catalyzes the
CC       calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of an acidic protein having phospholipase A2
CC       activity (B chain) and an A chain which weakly inhibits the B
CC       chain enzymatic activity but potentiates its lethal potency.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13607; Method=Electrospray; Range=17-138;
CC       Note=in Dsm-a1; Source=PubMed:17611171;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13812; Method=Electrospray; Range=17-138;
CC       Note=in Dsm-a1' which has only its protein sequence AA 17-27
CC       sequenced; Source=PubMed:17611171;
CC   -!- TOXIC DOSE: The lethal (intraperitoneal) dose of DbTx-B is
CC       estimated to be 0.5 ug/g, while that of the heterodimer is about
CC       0.1 ug/g.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not provoke hemorrhage (PubMed:7778130).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that impairs
CC       hemostasis. It weakly inhibits ADP-induced platelet aggregation
CC       when tested on platelet rich plasma from human and rabbit blood
CC       (15-25% of inhibition at 5-10 ug of enzyme), and dose-dependently
CC       inhibits blood coagulation, possibly by inhibiting thrombin
CC       activation. Exhibits high hydrolytic activities toward L-
CC       dipalmitoyl phosphatidylcholine. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-
CC       dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.

CC       138; Source=PubMed:15955061;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that shows a
CC       moderate inhibition of ADP-induced human platelet aggregation when
CC       tested on platelet rich plasma. Exhibits high hydrolytic
CC       activities and prefers the anionic micelles (dPPC with
CC       deoxycholate) to the zwitterionic micelles (dPPC with Triton X-
CC       100). PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-
CC       acyl groups in 3-sn-phosphoglycerides.

CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Is expressed more abundantly in juvenile than
CC       in adult vipers.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13734; Method=Electrospray; Range=17-138;
CC       Source=PubMed:12959640;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.
CC   -!- CAUTION: According to PubMed:12959640, T.stejnegeri was formerly
CC       named T.gramineus, supposing that this protein is the same as PLA-
CC       I from T.gramineus. They have been kept separated, because
CC       T.gramineus and T.stejnegeri are considered as being two different
CC       species (see http://reptile-database.org/).

RC   TISSUE=Venom;
RX   PubMed=17505111; DOI=10.1107/S0907444907016204;
RA   Gopalan G., Thwin M.M., Gopalakrishnakone P., Swaminathan K.;
RT   "Structural and pharmacological comparison of daboiatoxin from Daboia
RT   russelli siamensis with viperotoxin F and vipoxin from other vipers.";
RL   Acta Crystallogr. D 63:722-729(2007).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Monomer: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that shows
CC       a high PLA2 activity (2110 umol/min/mg).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Heterodimer (A and B chains): snake venom phospholipase
CC       A2 that shows a moderate PLA2 activity (1377 umol/min/mg). Acts as
CC       a presynaptic neurotoxin. In vivo, induces edema and produces
CC       neurotoxic symptoms in mice. It exhibits indirect hemolysis and a
CC       strong myonecrotic activity and is cytotoxic. PLA2 catalyzes the
CC       calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of an acidic protein having phospholipase A2
CC       activity (B chain) and an A chain which weakly inhibits the B
CC       chain enzymatic activity but potentiates its lethal potency.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- TOXIC DOSE: DbTx-A alone is non-lethal, even at doses as high as 2
CC       ug/g. The lethal (intraperitoneal) dose of the heterodimer is
CC       estimated to be about 0.1 ug/g.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not provoke hemorrhage (PubMed:7778130).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC       I(2), suggesting an increase of its potential anti-platelet
CC       activity in vivo. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-dependent hydrolysis
CC       of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13649.57; Method=MALDI; Range=17-138;
CC       Source=PubMed:16750518;
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not inhibit platelet aggregation when
CC       aggregation is induced by ADP, and does not induce aggregation of
CC       washed platelets. Does not induce changes on the principal
CC       platelet receptors (ITGA2, ITGA2B, GPIBA, SELP). In human
CC       umbilical-cord veins endothelial cells, does not induce
CC       detachment, does not interfere on nitric oxide release, and is
CC       neither apoptotic nor proliferative (PubMed:16750518).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that induces edema
CC       (activity that is inhibited by EDTA and dexamethasone), inhibits
CC       phospholipid-dependent collagen/ADP-induced platelet aggregation,
CC       possess hypotensive as well as anticoagulant activities. In
CC       addition, this enzyme shows bactericidal activity against E.coli
CC       and S.aureus. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-dependent hydrolysis of
CC       the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion per subunit.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by EDTA and BPB.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; non-covalently linked.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- TOXIC DOSE: LD(50) show no toxicity when injected into mice: 25
CC       mg/kg by intraperitoneal injection, 7.5 mg/kg by intravenous
CC       injection, and 0.5 mg/kg by intracerebroventricular injection.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: This enzyme has been found to be not myotoxic, not
CC       cytotoxic, not hemorrhagic and not lethal (PubMed:12167491).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that impairs
CC       hemostasis. It weakly inhibits ADP-induced platelet aggregation
CC       when tested on platelet rich plasma from human and rabbit blood
CC       (15-25% of inhibition at 5-10 ug of enzyme), and dose-dependently
CC       inhibits blood coagulation, possibly by inhibiting thrombin
CC       activation. Exhibits high hydrolytic activities toward L-
CC       dipalmitoyl phosphatidylcholine. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-
CC       dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.

CC       138; Source=PubMed:15955061;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

CC       ADP-(IC(50)=272 nM) and collagen-induced (IC(50)=518 nM) human

CC       micelles (dPPC with Triton X-100). PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-
CC       dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that has strong
CC       myotoxic activity with a low phospholipase A2 activity. PLA2
CC       catalyzes the calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in
CC       3-sn-phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Is abundantly expressed in Tokunoshima and Amami-
CC       Oshima P.flavoviridis venom, but is missing in Okinawa
CC       P.flavoviridis venom. It is thought that loss of BP-I in Okinawa
CC       P.flavoviridis is due to lack of necessity for a strong toxicity
CC       exerted by BP-I in the venom as far as they feed mostly on frogs.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. K49 sub-subfamily.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Binds calcium very weakly as one of the calcium-binding
CC       ligands is lost (Asp->Lys in position 64, which corresponds to
CC       'Lys-49' in the current nomenclature).

ID   PA2B_TRIPE              Reviewed;         138 AA.
AC   Q2YHJ7;

DE   RecName: Full=Basic phospholipase A2 Tpu-G6D49;
DE            Short=svPLA2;
DE            EC=3.1.1.4;
DE   AltName: Full=Phosphatidylcholine 2-acylhydrolase;
DE   Flags: Precursor;
OS   Trimeresurus puniceus (Flat-nosed pitviper).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Lepidosauria; Squamata; Bifurcata; Unidentata; Episquamata;
OC   Toxicofera; Serpentes; Colubroidea; Viperidae; Crotalinae;
OC   Trimeresurus.
OX   NCBI_TaxID=197218;
RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], PROTEIN SEQUENCE OF 17-39, FUNCTION,
RP   SUBUNIT, AND MASS SPECTROMETRY.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=15955061; DOI=10.1111/j.1742-4658.2005.04715.x;
RA   Wang Y.-M., Peng H.-F., Tsai I.-H.;
RT   "Unusual venom phospholipases A2 of two primitive tree vipers
RT   Trimeresurus puniceus and Trimeresurus borneensis.";
RL   FEBS J. 272:3015-3025(2005).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom phospholipase A2 (PLA2) that impairs
CC       hemostasis. It weakly inhibits ADP-induced platelet aggregation
CC       when tested on platelet rich plasma from human and rabbit blood
CC       (15-25% of inhibition at 5-10 ug of enzyme), and dose-dependently
CC       inhibits blood coagulation, possibly by inhibiting thrombin
CC       activation. Also induces local edema a few hours after injection
CC       in the hind foot. Exhibits high hydrolytic activities toward L-
CC       dipalmitoyl phosphatidylcholine. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-
CC       dependent hydrolysis of the 2-acyl groups in 3-sn-
CC       phosphoglycerides.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Phosphatidylcholine + H(2)O = 1-
CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=13912.8; Method=Electrospray; Range=17-
CC       138; Source=PubMed:15955061;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group II
CC       subfamily. D49 sub-subfamily.

ID   PA2HB_MICTN             Reviewed;         149 AA.
AC   G9I930;
DT   18-APR-2012, integrated into UniProtKB/Swiss-Prot.
DT   22-FEB-2012, sequence version 1.
DT   14-MAY-2014, entry version 17.
DE   RecName: Full=Basic phospholipase A2 homolog Tx-beta;
DE            Short=svPLA2 homolog;
DE   AltName: Full=MitTx-beta;
DE   Flags: Precursor;
OS   Micrurus tener tener (Texas coral snake).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Lepidosauria; Squamata; Bifurcata; Unidentata; Episquamata;
OC   Toxicofera; Serpentes; Colubroidea; Elapidae; Elapinae; Micrurus.
OX   NCBI_TaxID=1114302;
RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], PROTEIN SEQUENCE OF N-TERMINUS, FUNCTION,
RP   AND SUBUNIT.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=22094702; DOI=10.1038/nature10607;
RA   Bohlen C.J., Chesler A.T., Sharif-Naeini R., Medzihradszky K.F.,
RA   Zhou S., King D., Sanchez E.E., Burlingame A.L., Basbaum A.I.,
RA   Julius D.;
RT   "A heteromeric Texas coral snake toxin targets acid-sensing ion
RT   channels to produce pain.";
RL   Nature 479:410-414(2011).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Heterodimer: snake venom phospholipase that potently
CC       activates mouse H(+)-gated sodium channel ASIC1/ACCN2 (acid-
CC       sensitive ion channel 1) expressed in Xenopus oocytes. Both
CC       alternatively spliced isoforms ASIC1a and ASIC1b are activated,
CC       with a higher potency for ASIC1a (EC(50)=9.4 nM) vs ASIC1b
CC       (EC(50)=23 nM). The ASIC3/ACCN3 subtype is also sensitive to the
CC       heterodimer, but with a lower potency (EC(50)=830 nM). On
CC       ASIC2a/ACCN1, the toxin shows a very weak activation, but produces
CC       a remarkable potentiation (>100-fold) of protons when the
CC       extracellular pH drops below neutrality. The toxin interacts with
CC       the extracellular region of the channel, since responses are only
CC       observed in the outside-out configuration. In vivo, the
CC       heterodimer elicits robust pain-related behavior in mice by
CC       activation of ASIC1/ACCN2 channels on capsaicin-sensitive nerve
CC       fibers.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Monomer: does not have phospholipase A2 activity but may
CC       maintain some lipid-binding character from its PLA2 lineage, which
CC       could aid in effecting neuronal depolarization.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of an alpha and a beta chains.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: This toxin has been studied to probe molecular
CC       mechanisms underlying pain sensation. By targeting ASIC1/ACCN2, it
CC       reveals an unexpected contribution of this channel to nociception.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: The heterodimeric toxin does not affect
CC       ASIC2b/ACCN1, ASIC4/ACCN4, Kv2.1/KCNB1, Cav3.3/CACNA1I,
CC       ENaC/SCNN1A, TRPA1, TRPV1, TRPV3, TRPM8, P2X2/P2RX2, and 5-
CC       HT3/HTR3A channels (PubMed:22094702).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group I
CC       subfamily. K49 sub-subfamily.
CC   -!- WEB RESOURCE: Name=Protein Spotlight; Note=The poison in pain -
CC       Issue 140 of July 2012;
CC       URL="http://web.expasy.org/spotlight/back_issues/140";
CC   -----------------------------------------------------------------------
CC   Copyrighted by the UniProt Consortium, see http://www.uniprot.org/terms
CC   Distributed under the Creative Commons Attribution-NoDerivs License

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Scorpion venom phosholipase A2 (PLA2) that contains
CC       enzymatic activity, but does not inhibit ryanodine receptors in
CC       contrary to imperatoxin-1, another heterodimer of P.imperator
CC       venom. PLA2 catalyzes the calcium-dependent hydrolysis of the 2-
CC       acyl groups in 3-sn-phosphoglycerides.

CC       acylglycerophosphocholine + a carboxylate.

CC       subunit; disulfid-linked.

CC       145; Source=PubMed:10556514;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the phospholipase A2 family. Group III
CC       subfamily.
CC   -!- CAUTION: The sequence signal is uncertain for 2 reasons. Firstly,
CC       it contains 2 consecutive basic residues (Arg) that may indicate
CC       that this segment corresponds to the message for translating an

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Involved in the biosynthesis of conjugated triene-
CC       containing fatty acids. Catalyzes the isomerization of a wide
CC       range of substrates containing three or more methylene interrupted
CC       olefins into a Z,E,E conjugated triene functionality. May be
CC       involved in a stress tolerance mechanism as response to intertidal
CC       habitats with direct sunlight, desiccation and high temperature.
CC       In vitro substrates include arachidonic acid ((5Z,8Z,11Z,14Z)-
CC       eicosatetraenoic acid), EPA ((5Z,8Z, 11Z,14Z,17Z)-eicosapentaenoic
CC       acid), DHA ((4Z,7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z,19Z)-docosahexenoic acid), adrenic
CC       acid ((7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z)-docosatetraenoic acid), anandamide
CC       (arachidonyl-N-ethanolamide) and eicosatrienoic acid ((5Z,8Z,11Z)-
CC       eicosatrienoic acid). Gamma-linolenic acid (18:3 6Z,9Z,12Z) and
CC       dihomo-gamma-linolenic acid (20:3 8Z,11Z,14Z) are transformed into
CC       mixtures of conjugated diene and triene fatty acids, linoleic acid
CC       is only transformed to a conjugated diene.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: (5Z,8Z,11Z,14Z,17Z)-icosapentaenoate =
CC       (5Z,7E,9E,14Z,17Z)-icosapentaenoate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Flavin (Probable).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=1.9 uM for (4Z,7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z,19Z)-docosahexenoic acid;
CC         KM=17.0 uM for (7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z)-docosatetraenoic acid;
CC         KM=9.6 uM for (5Z,8Z, 11Z,14Z,17Z)-eicosapentaenoic acid;
CC         KM=25.5 uM for (5Z,8Z,11Z,14Z)-eicosatetraenoic acid;
CC         KM=52.8 uM for (5Z,8Z,11Z)-eicosatrienoic acid;
CC         KM=17.5 uM for arachidonyl-N-ethanolamide;
CC         Vmax=1.84 umol/min/mg enzyme with (4Z,7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z,19Z)-
CC         docosahexenoic acid as substrate;
CC         Vmax=1.1 umol/min/mg enzyme with (7Z,10Z,13Z,16Z)-
CC         docosatetraenoic acid as substrate;
CC         Vmax=6.0 umol/min/mg enzyme with (5Z,8Z, 11Z,14Z,17Z)-
CC         eicosapentaenoic acid as substrate;
CC         Vmax=2.78 umol/min/mg enzyme with (5Z,8Z,11Z,14Z)-
CC         eicosatetraenoic acid as substrate;
CC         Vmax=0.31 umol/min/mg enzyme with (5Z,8Z,11Z)-eicosatrienoic
CC         acid as substrate;
CC         Vmax=0.8 umol/min/mg enzyme with arachidonyl-N-ethanolamide as
CC         substrate;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is below pH 6.0 with (5Z,8Z,11Z,14Z,17Z)-
CC         eicosapentaenoic acid as substrate;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer (Probable).
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated.

RA   Nicholson E.M., Brunelle B.W., Richt J.A., Kehrli M.E. Jr.,

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [GENOMIC DNA], AND VARIANT H-TYPE BSE LYS-211.
RX   PubMed=18787697; DOI=10.1371/journal.ppat.1000156;
RA   Richt J.A., Hall S.M.;
RT   "BSE case associated with prion protein gene mutation.";
RL   PLoS Pathog. 4:E1000156-E1000156(2008).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: May play a role in neuronal development and synaptic
CC       plasticity. May be required for neuronal myelin sheath
CC       maintenance. May play a role in iron uptake and iron homeostasis.
CC       Soluble oligomers are toxic to cultured neuroblastoma cells and
CC       induce apoptosis (in vitro). Association with GPC1 (via its
CC       heparan sulfate chains) targets PRNP to lipid rafts. Also provides
CC       Cu(2+) or ZN(2+) for the ascorbate-mediated GPC1 deaminase
CC       degradation of its heparan sulfate side chains (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer and homodimer. Has a tendency to aggregate into
CC       amyloid fibrils containing a cross-beta spine, formed by a steric
CC       zipper of superposed beta-strands. Soluble oligomers may represent
CC       an intermediate stage on the path to fibril formation. Copper
CC       binding may promote oligomerization. Interacts with GRB2, APP,
CC       ERI3/PRNPIP and SYN1. Mislocalized cytosolically exposed PrP
CC       interacts with MGRN1; this interaction alters MGRN1 subcellular
CC       location and causes lysosomal enlargement (By similarity).
CC       Interacts with KIAA1191 (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Lipid-anchor, GPI-anchor (By
CC       similarity). Golgi apparatus (By similarity). Note=Targeted to
CC       lipid rafts via association with the heparan sulfate chains of
CC       GPC1. Colocates, in the presence of CU(2+), to vesicles in para-
CC       and perinuclear regions, where both proteins undergo
CC       internalization. Heparin displaces PRNP from lipid rafts and
CC       promotes endocytosis (By similarity).
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The normal, monomeric form has a mainly alpha-helical
CC       structure. The disease-associated, protease-resistant form forms
CC       amyloid fibrils containing a cross-beta spine, formed by a steric
CC       zipper of superposed beta-strands. Disease mutations may favor
CC       intermolecular contacts via short beta strands, and may thereby
CC       trigger oligomerization (By similarity).
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Contains an N-terminal region composed of octamer repeats.
CC       At low copper concentrations, the sidechains of His residues from
CC       three or four repeats contribute to the binding of a single copper
CC       ion. Alternatively, a copper ion can be bound by interaction with
CC       the sidechain and backbone amide nitrogen of a single His residue.
CC       The observed copper binding stoichiometry suggests that two repeat
CC       regions cooperate to stabilize the binding of a single copper ion.
CC       At higher copper concentrations, each octamer can bind one copper
CC       ion by interactions with the His side chain and Gly backbone
CC       atoms. A mixture of binding types may occur, especially in the
CC       case of octamer repeat expansion. Copper binding may stabilize the
CC       conformation of this region and may promote oligomerization (By
CC       similarity).
CC   -!- DISEASE: Note=Variations in PRNP are responsible of transmissible
CC       bovine spongiform encephalopathies (BSE), a class of
CC       neurodegenerative diseases that affect various mammals. These
CC       diseases are caused by abnormally folded prion proteins. BSE can
CC       be subdivided into at least three groups: classical, H-type and L-
CC       type, with the latter 2 collectively referred to as atypical BSE.
CC       Susceptibility or resistance to a BSE disease can be influenced by
CC       at least 3 factors related to the host prion protein: protein
CC       expression levels, number of octapeptide repeats, and specific
CC       polymorphisms. In cattle, as in humans, BSEs can occur as
CC       infectious, spontaneous and genetic diseases. The heritable
CC       variant Lys-211 can be the cause of genetic late onset H-type BSE.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the prion family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Major acute phase protein.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homohexamer; dimer of trimers. Can form amyloid fibrils
CC       after partial proteolysis; the native, undenatured protein does
CC       not form amyloid fibrils (in vitro). Apolipoprotein of the HDL
CC       complex. Binds to heparin.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the liver; secreted in plasma (at
CC       protein level).
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Upon cytokine stimulation.
CC   -!- PTM: This protein is the precursor of amyloid protein A, which is
CC       formed by the removal of approximately 24 residues from the C-
CC       terminal end.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11702; Mass_error=14; Method=MALDI;
CC       Range=19-122; Source=PubMed:12973732;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11682.7; Method=MALDI; Range=19-122;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11526.5; Method=MALDI; Range=20-122;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11439.6; Method=MALDI; Range=21-122;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11363.6; Method=MALDI; Range=20-121;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=11235.6; Method=MALDI; Range=20-120;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=10872.6; Method=MALDI; Range=22-119;
CC       Source=PubMed:12606051;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=8337.5; Mass_error=0.8;
CC       Method=Electrospray; Range=19-94; Note=With variants Ala-70, Val-
CC       75, Asn-78 and 86-Leu-Thr-87; Source=PubMed:1463770;
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=8390.9; Mass_error=0.2;
CC       Method=Electrospray; Range=19-94; Note=With variant Ala-70;
CC       Source=PubMed:1463770;
CC   -!- POLYMORPHISM: At least 5 different SAA1 alleles have been
CC       described: SAA1.1 (SAA1alpha), SAA1.2 (SAA1beta), SAA1.3
CC       (SAA1gamma), SAA1.4 (SAA1delta), SAA1.5 (also named SAA1beta but
CC       which differs from SAA1.2). We use here the revised nomenclature
CC       described in PubMed:10211414. The sequence shown is that of
CC       SAA1.1.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Note=Reactive, secondary amyloidosis is characterized by
CC       the extracellular accumulation in various tissues of the SAA1
CC       protein. These deposits are highly insoluble and resistant to
CC       proteolysis; they disrupt tissue structure and compromise
CC       function.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Note=Elevated serum SAA1 protein levels may be associated
CC       with lung cancer.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the SAA family.

OX   NCBI_TaxID=242841;
RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], PROTEIN SEQUENCE OF 24-44, FUNCTION, AND
RP   SUBUNIT.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=21256857; DOI=10.1016/j.toxicon.2011.01.010;
RA   Chen Z., Wu J., Zhang Y., Yang X., Yu G., Zhu S., Lee W., Lu Q.,
RA   Zhang Y.;
RT   "A novel platelet glycoprotein Ib-binding protein with human platelet
RT   aggregation-inhibiting activity from Trimeresurus jerdonii venom.";
RL   Toxicon 57:672-679(2011).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snaclec that dose-dependently inhibits platelet
CC       aggregation induced by ristocetin or low-dose thrombin, but not by
CC       high-dose thrombin. Binds to GPIbalpha (GP1BA). In vivo, also
CC       dose-dependently induces thrombocytopenia of mice and platelet
CC       counts remains at very low level even after 18 hours intravenous
CC       injection.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of subunits alpha and beta; disulfide-linked.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not induce platelet aggregation in either
CC       platelet rich plasma or washed platelets under high-dose
CC       conditions. Does not inhibit platelet aggregation induced by high-
CC       dose thrombin. Does not react with polyclonal anti-GPVI and anti-
CC       GPIIb antibodies (PubMed:21256857).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the snaclec family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 C-type lectin domain.

CC   Distributed under the Creative Commons Attribution-NoDerivs License

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Beta toxins bind voltage-independently at site-4 of
CC       sodium channels (Nav) and shift the voltage of activation toward
CC       more negative potentials thereby affecting sodium channel
CC       activation and promoting spontaneous and repetitive firing. This
CC       toxin is lethal to insects (A.domestica). It is not toxic to mice
CC       and does not affect mammal F11 sodium channels.

RA   Shoyama Y., Tamada T., Kurihara K., Takeuchi A., Taura F., Arai S.,
RA   Blaber M., Shoyama Y., Morimoto S., Kuroki R.;
RT   "Structure and function of delta(1)-tetrahydrocannabinolic acid (THCA)
RT   synthase, the enzyme controlling the psychoactivity of Cannabis
RT   sativa.";
RL   J. Mol. Biol. 423:96-105(2012).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the oxidative cyclization of the monoterpene
CC       moiety in cannabigerolic acid (CBGA), producing delta(9)-
CC       tetrahydrocannabinolate (THCA), the major cannabioid in drug-type
CC       Cannabis plants. Can also use cannabinerolic acid as substrate,
CC       but not cannabigerol or cannabinerol.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Cannabigerolate + O(2) = Delta(9)-
CC       tetrahydrocannabinolate + H(2)O(2).
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by Hg(2+).
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=134 uM for cannabigerolic acid;
CC         KM=254 uM for cannabinerolic acid;
CC         Vmax=2.68 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with cannabigerolic acid as
CC         substrate;
CC         Vmax=0.37 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with cannabinerolic acid as
CC         substrate;
CC         Note=kcat is 0.30 sec(-1) for cannabigerolate;
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 5.5-6.0;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted. Secreted, extracellular space,
CC       apoplast. Note=Sorted from the secretory cells into the storage
CC       cavity of glandular trichomes.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the secretory cells of glandular
CC       trichomes.
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated when produced in an heterologous system. The
CC       deglycosylated THCA synthase has more catalytic activity than the
CC       glycosylated form.
CC   -!- POLYMORPHISM: Several isoforms of the active
CC       tetrahydrocannabinolic acid synthase found in the 'drug-type'
CC       cannabis plants exist due to polymorphism.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: THCA synthase might contribute to the self-defense
CC       of Cannabis plants by producing both THCA and hydrogen peroxide,
CC       but since these reaction products are toxic to the plant itself,
CC       THCA synthase must be secreted from secretory cells into the
CC       storage cavity to avoid cellular damage.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the oxygen-dependent FAD-linked
CC       oxidoreductase family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 FAD-binding PCMH-type domain.

CC   Distributed under the Creative Commons Attribution-NoDerivs License

RN   [9]
RP   SUBCELLULAR LOCATION, TISSUE SPECIFICITY, DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE, AND
RP   GLYCOSYLATION BY PGANT3.
RX   PubMed=20371600; DOI=10.1074/jbc.M109.098145;
RA   Zhang L., Tran D.T., Ten Hagen K.G.;
RT   "An O-glycosyltransferase promotes cell adhesion during development by
RT   influencing secretion of an extracellular matrix integrin ligand.";
RL   J. Biol. Chem. 285:19491-19501(2010).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Functions as a ligand for integrin alpha-PS2/beta-PS.
CC       Required in larvae for proper muscle structure and function.
CC       Involved in the regulation of cell adhesion during wing
CC       development.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted, extracellular space, extracellular
CC       matrix. Note=Localizes to the basal surface of the dorsoventral
CC       cell layer interface during pupal wing development.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: In embryos, expressed in the apodemes (muscle
CC       attachment sites) of the major longitudinal muscles 4, 6, 7, 12
CC       and 13 and the wide dorsal oblique muscles 9 and 10, in hemocytes,
CC       in fat body cells, in basement membranes surrounding the gut and
CC       in the commissures of the ventral nerve cord. Expressed in larval
CC       imaginal wing disk and in pupal wing. In adult flies, expressed in
CC       the jump muscle (at protein level).
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed throughout embryogenesis; first
CC       appears at 8-10 hours. Detected in larval and pupal stages (at
CC       protein level). Transcripts are first detected at 6-8 hours of
CC       development, expression peaks at 12-14 hours and then declines by
CC       the end of embryogenesis.
CC   -!- PTM: O-glycosylation by pgant3 is required for proper secretion
CC       and localization to the basal cell layer interface during wing
CC       development.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Pupal lethal with about 1% escapers. In
CC       mutant larvae, muscles 6 and 7 appear stringy and not anchored to
CC       other muscles or the epidermis, often these muscles are missing or
CC       unrecognizable. Sites where muscles 3, 4, 5, 8 and 16 come
CC       together are rarely recognizable and large gaps between muscles 9
CC       and 10 can be observed. Muscle contraction waves that transverse
CC       the length of the larvae and are responsible for locomotion are
CC       much slower in mutant larvae. Mutant pupae are longer than wild
CC       type pupae. Mutant adult flies present elongated abdomen and wings
CC       with altered shapes and sizes.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Appears to be involved in vesicular protein trafficking,
CC       mainly in the early secretory pathway. In COPI vesicle-mediated
CC       retrograde transport involved in the coatomer recruitment to
CC       membranes of the early secretory pathway. Increases coatomer-
CC       dependent activity of ARFGAP2. Thought to play a crucial role in
CC       the specific retention of p24 complexes in cis-Golgi membranes;
CC       specifically contributes to the coupled localization of TMED2 and
CC       TMED10 in the cis-Golgi network. May be involved in organization
CC       of intracellular membranes, such as of the ER-Golgi intermediate
CC       compartment and the Golgi apparatus. Involved in ER localization
CC       of PTPN2 (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer and homodimer in endoplasmic reticulum.
CC       Predominantly monomeric and to lesser extent homodimeric in
CC       endoplasmic reticulum-Golgi intermediate compartment and cis-Golgi
CC       network. Probably oligomerizes with other members of the
CC       EMP24/GP25L family such as TMED2, TMED7 and TMED10. Interacts with
CC       TMED5. Interacts (via C-terminus) with COPG1; the interaction
CC       involves dimeric TMED9. Interacts with PTPN2 and SPAST (By
CC       similarity). Interacts with STX17; the interaction is direct.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q9R064:Gorasp2; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-920903, EBI-4422912;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Endoplasmic reticulum membrane; Single-pass
CC       type I membrane protein. Golgi apparatus, cis-Golgi network
CC       membrane; Single-pass type I membrane protein. Endoplasmic
CC       reticulum-Golgi intermediate compartment membrane; Single-pass
CC       type I membrane protein. Golgi apparatus, trans-Golgi network
CC       membrane; Single-pass type I membrane protein (By similarity).
CC       Note=Cycles between compartments of the early secretatory pathway.
CC   -!- PTM: N-linked glycosylated containing high mannose (By
CC       similarity).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the EMP24/GP25L family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 GOLD domain.

RP   X-RAY CRYSTALLOGRAPHY (2.01 ANGSTROMS) OF 21-135 OF MUTANT
RP   50-GLU--LEU-55, INTERACTION WITH CED-1, HOMODIMERIZATION, SUBCELLULAR
RP   LOCATION, DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE, AND MUTAGENESIS OF ASP-36; GLU-38;

RP   131-TYR--TYR-135.
RX   PubMed=22713871; DOI=10.1101/gad.187815.112;
RA   Kang Y., Zhao D., Liang H., Liu B., Zhang Y., Liu Q., Wang X., Liu Y.;
RT   "Structural study of TTR-52 reveals the mechanism by which a bridging
RT   molecule mediates apoptotic cell engulfment.";
RL   Genes Dev. 26:1339-1350(2012).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Plays a role as a bridging molecule that mediates
CC       recognition and engulfment of apoptotic cells by cross-linking the
CC       surface-exposed phosphatidylserine with the extracellular domain
CC       of the phagocyte receptor ced-1. Important for the generation of
CC       extracellular phosphatidylserine vesicles that promote loss of the
CC       exoplasmic leaflet from apoptotic cells in a time-dependent
CC       manner. Required for the exposure of exoplasmic leaflet on the
CC       phagocytic cells surrounding the apoptotic cells. Does not affect
CC       the phosphatidylserine externalization in living cells. May play a
CC       role in mediating transfer of phosphatidylserine from
CC       phosphatidylserine vesicles to ced-1 bearing phagocytes or
CC       alternatively result in the activation of a phosphatidylserine
CC       transporter in the phagocyte that promotes phosphatidylserine
CC       externalization.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer. Interacts with ced-1. Interacts with nrf-5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted. Cell surface. Note=Detected almost
CC       exclusively on the surface of apoptotic cells. In some embryos,
CC       also observed on surface of cells adjacent to dying cells.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the intestine cells.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Loses ability to bind apoptotic cells and
CC       results in reduced ability of cell corpse engulfment.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the nematode transthyretin-like family.

CC       vivo, induces severe neurotoxic events in mice such as
CC       excitability and convulsions, leading to the death of the animals
CC       within a few minutes after injection. Does not show toxicity in
CC       insects and crustaceans.

CC       injection.

CC       voltage-gated sodium channels (PubMed:22819772).

RA   McCleary R.J., Kerkkamp H.M., Vos R.A., Guerreiro I., Calvete J.J.,
RA   Wuster W., Woods A.E., Logan J.M., Harrison R.A., Castoe T.A.,
RA   de Koning A.P., Pollock D.D., Yandell M., Calderon D., Renjifo C.,
RA   Currier R.B., Salgado D., Pla D., Sanz L., Hyder A.S., Ribeiro J.M.,
RA   Arntzen J.W., van den Thillart G.E., Boetzer M., Pirovano W.,
RA   Dirks R.P., Spaink H.P., Duboule D., McGlinn E., Kini R.M.,
RA   Richardson M.K.;
RT   "The king cobra genome reveals dynamic gene evolution and adaptation
RT   in the snake venom system.";
RL   Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. U.S.A. 110:20651-20656(2013).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Complement-activating protein in cobra venom. It is a
CC       structural and functional analog of complement component C3b, the
CC       activated form of C3. It binds factor B (CFB), which is
CC       subsequently cleaved by factor D (CFD) to form the bimolecular
CC       complex OVF/Bb. OVF/Bb is a C3/C5 convertase that cleaves both
CC       complement components C3 and C5. Structurally, it resembles the
CC       C3b degradation product C3c, which is not able to form a C3/C5
CC       convertase. Unlike C3b/Bb, OVF/Bb is a stable complex and
CC       completely resistant to the actions of complement regulatory
CC       factors H (CFH) and I (CFI). Therefore, OVF continuously activates
CC       complement (By similarity). As a result, OVF exhibits complement-
CC       depleting activity.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterotrimer of alpha, beta and gamma chains; disulfide-
CC       linked. May be active with factor B in the presence of factor D.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: First processed by the removal of 4 Arg residues by furin-
CC       type protease, forming two chains, alpha and gamma/beta precursor,
CC       linked by a disulfide bond. Probably, a cobrin-like protease
CC       cleaves the C3a-like domain and then the C3d-like domain,
CC       generating the mature venom factor (OVF) (By similarity).
CC   -!- PTM: The beta chain is not glycosylated (PubMed:22561424).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom complement C3 homolog family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 anaphylatoxin-like domain.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 NTR domain.

OS   Micrurus tener tener (Texas coral snake).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;

RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], PARTIAL PROTEIN SEQUENCE, FUNCTION,
RP   SUBUNIT, AND PYROGLUTAMATE FORMATION AT GLN-25.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=22094702; DOI=10.1038/nature10607;
RA   Bohlen C.J., Chesler A.T., Sharif-Naeini R., Medzihradszky K.F.,
RA   Zhou S., King D., Sanchez E.E., Burlingame A.L., Basbaum A.I.,
RA   Julius D.;
RT   "A heteromeric Texas coral snake toxin targets acid-sensing ion
RT   channels to produce pain.";
RL   Nature 479:410-414(2011).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: This heterodimeric toxin potently activates mouse acid-
CC       sensing ion channel ASIC1/ACCN2 expressed in Xenopus oocytes. Both
CC       alternatively spliced isoforms ASIC1a and ASIC1b are activated,
CC       with a higher potency for ASIC1a (EC(50)=9.4 nM) vs ASIC1b
CC       (EC(50)=23 nM). The ASIC3/ACCN3 subtype is also sensitive to the
CC       heterodimer, but with a lower potency (EC(50)=830 nM). On
CC       ASIC2a/ACCN1, the toxin shows a very weak activation, but produces
CC       a remarkable potentiation (>100-fold) of protons when the
CC       extracellular pH drops below neutrality. The toxin interacts with
CC       the extracellular region of the channel, since responses are only
CC       observed in the outside-out configuration. In vivo, the
CC       heterodimer elicits robust pain-related behavior in mice by
CC       activation of ASIC1/ACCN2 channels on capsaicin-sensitive nerve
CC       fibers.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of an alpha and a beta chains.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: This toxin has been studied to probe molecular
CC       mechanisms underlying pain sensation. By targeting ASIC1/ACCN2, it
CC       reveals an unexpected contribution of this channel to nociception
CC       (PubMed:22094702).
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: The heterodimeric toxin does not affect
CC       ASIC2b/ACCN1, ASIC4/ACCN4, Kv2.1/KCNB1, Cav3.3/CACNA1I,
CC       ENaC/SCNN1A, TRPA1, TRPV1, TRPV3, TRPM8, P2X2/P2RX2, and 5-
CC       HT3/HTR3A channels (PubMed:22094702).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom Kunitz-type family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 BPTI/Kunitz inhibitor domain.

ID   VKTK1_DABRR             Reviewed;          90 AA.
AC   H6VC05;
DT   01-MAY-2013, integrated into UniProtKB/Swiss-Prot.
DT   18-APR-2012, sequence version 1.
DT   11-JUN-2014, entry version 14.
DE   RecName: Full=Kunitz-type serine protease inhibitor DrKIn-I;
DE   AltName: Full=Daboia russelii Kunitz Inhibitor-I;
DE   Flags: Precursor;
OS   Daboia russelii (Russel's viper) (Vipera russelii).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Lepidosauria; Squamata; Bifurcata; Unidentata; Episquamata;
OC   Toxicofera; Serpentes; Colubroidea; Viperidae; Viperinae; Daboia.
OX   NCBI_TaxID=31159;
RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], FUNCTION, BIOASSAY, PYROGLUTAMATE
RP   FORMATION AT GLN-25, AND MASS SPECTROMETRY.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=22416129; DOI=10.1074/jbc.M111.323063;
RA   Cheng A.C., Wu H.L., Shi G.Y., Tsai I.H.;
RT   "A novel heparin-dependent inhibitor of activated protein C that
RT   potentiates consumptive coagulopathy in Russell's viper
RT   envenomation.";
RL   J. Biol. Chem. 287:15739-15748(2012).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Serine protease inhibitor. Inhibits activated protein C
CC       (APC) with an IC(50) of 3.5 nM in the presence of heparin (to
CC       which it strongly binds) and an IC(50) of 88.9 nM in its absence.
CC       Other targets are also significantly inhibited in presence of
CC       heparin: trypsin (PRSS1) (45%), coagulation FXIa (F11) (40%), and
CC       plasmin (PLG) (70%). In vivo, synergizes with RVV-X in promoting
CC       coagulation in mice and by extension in Russell's viper bite
CC       patients.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=7548.9; Method=MALDI; Range=25-90;
CC       Source=PubMed:22416129;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom Kunitz-type family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 BPTI/Kunitz inhibitor domain.

CC   Distributed under the Creative Commons Attribution-NoDerivs License
CC   -----------------------------------------------------------------------

ID   VKTK2_DABRR             Reviewed;          84 AA.
AC   H6VC06;
DT   01-MAY-2013, integrated into UniProtKB/Swiss-Prot.
DT   18-APR-2012, sequence version 1.
DT   11-JUN-2014, entry version 13.
DE   RecName: Full=Kunitz-type serine protease inhibitor DrKIn-II;
DE   AltName: Full=Daboia russelii Kunitz Inhibitor-II;
DE   Flags: Precursor;
OS   Daboia russelii (Russel's viper) (Vipera russelii).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Lepidosauria; Squamata; Bifurcata; Unidentata; Episquamata;
OC   Toxicofera; Serpentes; Colubroidea; Viperidae; Viperinae; Daboia.
OX   NCBI_TaxID=31159;
RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], FUNCTION, AND MASS SPECTROMETRY.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=22416129; DOI=10.1074/jbc.M111.323063;
RA   Cheng A.C., Wu H.L., Shi G.Y., Tsai I.H.;
RT   "A novel heparin-dependent inhibitor of activated protein C that
RT   potentiates consumptive coagulopathy in Russell's viper
RT   envenomation.";
RL   J. Biol. Chem. 287:15739-15748(2012).
RN   [2]
RP   FUNCTION.
RC   TISSUE=Venom;
RX   PubMed=23999090; DOI=10.1016/j.bbagen.2013.08.019;
RA   Cheng A.C., Tsai I.H.;
RT   "Functional characterization of a slow and tight-binding inhibitor of
RT   plasmin isolated from Russell's viper venom.";
RL   Biochim. Biophys. Acta 1840:153-159(2014).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Serine protease inhibitor that inhibits plasmin (90%)
CC       (Ki=0.19 nM), trypsin (70%), FXIa/F11 (37%) (Ki=6 nM) and FXa/F10
CC       (20%), and prolonges the activated partial thromboplastin time.
CC       This antifibrinolytic property has been confirmed by a fibrin
CC       plate assay. Shows less antifibrinolytic activity that aprotinin.
CC       In vivo, reduces the bleeding time in a murine bleeding model, and
CC       prevents the increase of fibrin(ogen) degradation products in
CC       coagulation-stimulated mice.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=6940.3; Method=MALDI; Range=25-84;
CC       Source=PubMed:22416129;
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not inhibit activated protein C (APC), in
CC       absence or presence of heparin. This is due to the absence of
CC       heparin-binding motifs. Consequently, heparin is unable to enhance
CC       the inhibition of activated protein C (APC) by this protein, as it
CC       does for DrKIn-I (PubMed:22416129). Does not inhibit tissue
CC       plasminogen activator (tPA/PLAT) and urokinase-type plasminogen
CC       activator (uPA/PLAU). Does not prolong the prothrombin time
CC       (PubMed:23999090).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom Kunitz-type family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 BPTI/Kunitz inhibitor domain.

CC   Distributed under the Creative Commons Attribution-NoDerivs License

OS   lebetina transmediterranea).

RN   [1]
RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA], FUNCTION, SUBUNIT, PYROGLUTAMATE FORMATION
RP   AT GLN-25, AND MASS SPECTROMETRY.
RC   TISSUE=Venom, and Venom gland;
RX   PubMed=23262217; DOI=10.1016/j.matbio.2012.11.015;
RA   Morjen M., Kallech-Ziri O., Bazaa A., Othman H., Mabrouk K.,
RA   Zouari-Kessentini R., Sanz L., Calvete J.J., Srairi-Abid N.,
RA   El Ayeb M., Luis J., Marrakchi N.;
RT   "PIVL, a new serine protease inhibitor from Macrovipera lebetina
RT   transmediterranea venom, impairs motility of human glioblastoma
RT   cells.";
RL   Matrix Biol. 32:52-62(2013).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Serine protease inhibitor that inhibits trypsin.
CC       Exhibits an anti-tumor effect and displays integrin inhibitory
CC       activity without being cytotoxic. Is able to dose-dependently
CC       inhibit the adhesion, migration and invasion of human glioblastoma
CC       U87 cells. Also impairs the function of alphavbeta3 and to a
CC       lesser extent, the activity of alphavbeta6, alphavbeta5,
CC       alpha1beta1 and alpha5beta1 integrins.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=7691.7; Method=MALDI; Range=25-91;
CC       Note=Average mass; Source=PubMed:23262217;
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not inhibit chymotrypsin (PubMed:23262217).
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: When intracerebroventricularly injected into mice,
CC       does not cause any toxic symptoms until a dose of 2 ug
CC       (PubMed:23262217).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom Kunitz-type family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 BPTI/Kunitz inhibitor domain.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Cell wall protein which plays an anti-adhesive role and
CC       promotes dispersal of yeast forms, which allows the organism to
CC       seek new sites for colonization.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted. Secreted, cell wall. Membrane;
CC       Lipid-anchor, GPI-anchor (Potential). Note=In yeast cultures, is
CC       linked covalently to glucans of the wall matrix, but, as cultures
CC       approach stationary phase, accumulates in the medium and is
CC       extractable from cells with disulfide-reducing agents. Removed
CC       from the cell wall by proteolytic cleavage by SAP9 and SAP10.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Expression is greatest during yeast exponential-phase
CC       growth, but down-regulated in stationary phase and upon
CC       filamentation. Expression is also increased during growth in
CC       hypoxic conditions. Expression decreases in biofilm cultures and
CC       becomes undetectable through late stage biofilm formation. Up-
CC       regulated when the extracellular phosphate concentration is low or
CC       in presence of Cis-2-dodecenoic acid (BDSF). Repressed during cell
CC       wall regeneration. Expression is positively regulated by EFG1 and
CC       EFH1, and negatively regulated by SSN6 and SSK1.
CC   -!- PTM: The GPI-anchor is attached to the protein in the endoplasmic
CC       reticulum and serves to target the protein to the cell surface.
CC       There, the glucosamine-inositol phospholipid moiety is cleaved off
CC       and the GPI-modified mannoprotein is covalently attached via its
CC       lipidless GPI glycan remnant to the 1,6-beta-glucan of the outer
CC       cell wall layer.
CC   -!- PTM: Cleaved by SAP9 and SAP10, which leads to its release from
CC       the cell wall.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Leads to increased adhesion and biofilm
CC       formation.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the flocculin family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Component of the zona pellucida, which mediates species-
CC       specific sperm binding. Directly binds to sperm. Important for egg
CC       fertilization.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer. Forms higher oligomers, once its C-terminus
CC       has been proteolytically removed. Forms heterooligomers with other
CC       zona pellucida glycoproteins (By similarity).
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Self; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-2942236, EBI-2942236;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Processed zona pellucida sperm-binding
CC       protein 3: Secreted, extracellular space, extracellular matrix.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Single-pass type I membrane
CC       protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Detected in the ovarian perivitteline layer.
CC       Detected in granulosa cells in ovarian follicle (at protein
CC       level). Detected in granulosa cells in ovarian follicle.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The ZP domain is involved in the polymerization of the ZP
CC       proteins to form the zona pellucida (By similarity).
CC   -!- PTM: Proteolytically cleaved before the transmembrane segment to
CC       yield the secreted ectodomain incorporated in the zona pellucida.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated.
CC   -!- PTM: O-glycosylated. O-glycosylation at Thr-168 is important for
CC       efficient interaction with the sperm head.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ZP domain family. ZPC subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 ZP domain.
